1108Google apps, sites, and devices, like Search, YouTube, and Google Home</li>

1109<li>

1110Platforms like the Chrome browser and Android operating system</li>

1111<li>

1112Products that are integrated into third-party apps and sites, like ads and embedded Google Maps</li>

1113</ul>

1114<p>

1115You can use our services in a variety of ways to manage your privacy. For example, you can sign up for a Google Account if you want to create and manage content like emails and photos, or see more relevant search results. And you can use many Google services when you’re signed out or without creating an account at all, like searching on Google or watching YouTube videos. You can also choose to browse the web privately using Chrome in Incognito mode. And across our services, you can adjust your privacy settings to control what we collect and how your information is used.</p>

1116<p>

1118key terms</a>

1119. And if you have any questions about this Privacy Policy, you can <a href="https://support.google.com/policies?p=privpol_privts" class="N6CPUe" target="_blank">

1120contact us</a>

1136<h1>

1137Information Google collects</h1>

1138<p class="vxK8q">

1139We want you to understand the types of information we collect as you use our services</p>

1140<p>

1141We collect information to provide better services to all our users — from figuring out basic stuff like which language you speak, to more complex things like which <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-useful-ads" data-name="useful-ads" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1142ads you’ll find most useful</a>

1143, <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-people-online" data-name="people-online" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1144the people who matter most to you online</a>

1145, or which YouTube videos you might like. The information Google collects, and how that information is used, depends on how you use our services and how you manage your privacy controls.</p>

1146<p>

1147When you’re not signed in to a Google Account, we store the information we collect with <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-unique-id" data-name="unique-id" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1148unique identifiers</a>

1149 tied to the browser, application, or <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-device" data-name="device" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1150device</a>

1151 you’re using. This helps us do things like maintain your language preferences across browsing sessions.</p>

1152<p>

1153When you’re signed in, we also collect information that we store with your Google Account, which we treat as <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-personal-info" data-name="personal-info" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1154personal information</a>

1155.</p>

1156<h2>

1157Things you create or provide to us</h2>

1158<div class="pjyxF ">

1159<img class="zZLvvc" alt="" src="https://www.gstatic.com/policies/privacy/d1b68e2cd423aba52d74f02573df2d2d.svg"/>

1160</div>

1161<p>

1162When you create a Google Account, you provide us with <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-personal-info" data-name="personal-info" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1163personal information</a>

1164 that includes your name and a password. You can also choose to add a <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-phone-number" data-name="phone-number" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1165phone number</a>

1166 or <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-payment-info" data-name="payment-info" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1167payment information</a>

1168 to your account. Even if you aren’t signed in to a Google Account, you might choose to provide us with information — like an email address to receive updates about our services.</p>

1169<p>

1170We also collect the content you create, upload, or receive from others when using our services. This includes things like email you write and receive, photos and videos you save, docs and spreadsheets you create, and comments you make on YouTube videos.</p>

1171<h2>

1172Information we collect as you use our services</h2>

1173<h3>

1174Your apps, browsers & devices</h3>

1175<div class="pjyxF ">

1176<img class="zZLvvc" alt="" src="https://www.gstatic.com/policies/privacy/e79ea0ed464fc8952d5b5582f9f9ae53.svg"/>

1177</div>

1178<p>

1179We collect information about the apps, browsers, and <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-devices" data-name="devices" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1180devices</a>

1181 you use to access Google services, which helps us provide features like automatic product updates and dimming your screen if your battery runs low.</p>

1182<p>

1183The information we collect includes <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-unique-id" data-name="unique-id" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1184unique identifiers</a>

1185, browser type and settings, device type and settings, operating system, mobile network information including carrier name and phone number, and application version number. We also collect information about the interaction of your apps, browsers, and devices with our services, including <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-ip" data-name="ip" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1186IP address</a>

1187, crash reports, system activity, and the date, time, and <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-referrer-url" data-name="referrer-url" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1188referrer URL</a>

1189 of your request.</p>

1190<p>

1191We collect this information when a Google service on your device contacts our servers — for example, when you install an app from the Play Store or when a service checks for automatic updates. If you’re using an <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-android-device" data-name="android-device" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1192Android device with Google apps</a>

1193, your device periodically contacts Google servers to provide information about your device and connection to our services. This information includes things like your device type, carrier name, crash reports, and which apps you've installed.</p>

1194<h3>

1195Your activity</h3>

1196<div class="pjyxF ">

1197<img class="zZLvvc" alt="" src="https://www.gstatic.com/policies/privacy/39b031d352a2e1586cf50ac7f2bbc18b.svg"/>

1198</div>

1199<p>

1200We collect information about your activity in our services, which we use to do things like recommend a YouTube video you might like. The activity information we collect may include:</p>

1201<ul>

1202<li>

1203Terms you search for</li>

1204<li>

1205Videos you watch</li>

1206<li>

1207<a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-content-views" data-name="content-views" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1208Views and interactions with content and ads</a>

1209</li>

1210<li>

1211Voice and audio information when you use audio features</li>

1212<li>

1213Purchase activity</li>

1214<li>

1215People with whom you communicate or share content</li>

1216<li>

1217Activity on third-party sites and apps that use our services</li>

1218<li>

1219Chrome browsing history you’ve <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-chrome-sync" data-name="chrome-sync" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1220synced with your Google Account</a>

1221</li>

1222</ul>

1223<p>

1224If you use our <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-calls-messages" data-name="calls-messages" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1225services to make and receive calls or send and receive messages</a>

1226, we may collect call and message log information like your phone number, calling-party number, receiving-party number, forwarding numbers, sender and recipient email address, time and date of calls and messages, duration of calls, routing information, and types and volumes of calls and messages.</p>

1227<p>

1228You can visit your Google Account to find and manage activity information that’s saved in your account.</p>

1229<div class="h0yEnd">

1230<div class="IN2z4b">

1231<img class="mZPFM " alt="" src="https://www.gstatic.com/policies/privacy/0d6da8d8c44e7e3ee95c4d56c19f04e1.svg"/>

1232</div>

1234<p class="n8ZyWe">

1235<a href="https://myaccount.google.com/?utm_source=pp" class="ky8S2">

1236Go to Google Account</a>

1237</p>

1240<h3>

1241Your location information</h3>

1242<div class="pjyxF ">

1243<img class="zZLvvc" alt="" src="https://www.gstatic.com/policies/privacy/4c5ee41d52605ff6f43538d46a1c0d35.svg"/>

1244</div>

1245<p>

1246We collect information about your location when you use our services, which helps us offer features like driving directions for your weekend getaway or showtimes for movies playing near you.</p>

1247<p>

1248Your location can be determined with varying degrees of accuracy by:</p>

1249<ul>

1250<li>

1251GPS</li>

1252<li>

1253<a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-ip" data-name="ip" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1254IP address</a>

1255</li>

1256<li>

1257<a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-sensor-data" data-name="sensor-data" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1258Sensor data from your device</a>

1259</li>

1260<li>

1261<a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-near-device" data-name="near-device" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1262Information about things near your device</a>

1263, such as Wi-Fi access points, cell towers, and Bluetooth-enabled devices</li>

1264</ul>

1265<p>

1266The types of location data we collect depend in part on your device and account settings. For example, you can <a href="https://support.google.com/accounts?p=privpol_location" class="N6CPUe" target="_blank">

1267turn your Android device’s location on or off</a>

1268 using the device’s settings app. You can also turn on <a href="https://support.google.com/accounts?p=privpol_lochistory" class="N6CPUe" target="_blank">

1269Location History</a>

1270 if you want to create a private map of where you go with your signed-in devices.</p>

1271<hr/>

1272<p>

1273In some circumstances, Google also collects information about you from <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-sources" data-name="sources" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1274publicly accessible sources</a>

1275. For example, if your name appears in your local newspaper, Google’s Search engine may index that article and display it to other people if they search for your name. We may also collect information about you from trusted partners, such as directory services who provide us with business information to be displayed on Google’s services, marketing partners who provide us with information about potential customers of our business services, and security partners who provide us with information to <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-against-abuse" data-name="against-abuse" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1276protect against abuse</a>

1277. We also receive information from advertisers to provide <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-ad-services" data-name="ad-services" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1278advertising and research services on their behalf</a>

1279.</p>

1280<p>

1281We use various technologies to collect and store information, including <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-cookies" data-name="cookies" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1282cookies</a>

1283, <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-pixel" data-name="pixel" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1284pixel tags</a>

1285, local storage, such as <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-browser-storage" data-name="browser-storage" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1286browser web storage</a>

1287 or <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-application-data-cache" data-name="application-data-cache" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1288application data caches</a>

1289, databases, and <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-server-logs" data-name="server-logs" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1290server logs</a>

1291.</p>

1306<h1>

1307Why Google collects data</h1>

1308<p class="vxK8q">

1309We use data to build better services</p>

1310<p>

1311We use the information we collect from all our services for the following purposes:</p>

1312<h3>

1313Provide our services</h3>

1314<div class="pjyxF ">

1315<img class="zZLvvc" alt="" src="https://www.gstatic.com/policies/privacy/b18d13e9ea8a362642b7d25bce665039.svg"/>

1316</div>

1317<p>

1318We use your information to <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-deliver-services" data-name="deliver-services" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1319deliver our services</a>

1320, like processing the terms you search for in order to return results or helping you share content by suggesting recipients from your contacts.<h3>

1321Maintain & improve our services</h3>

1322<div class="pjyxF ">

1323<img class="zZLvvc" alt="" src="https://www.gstatic.com/policies/privacy/4165cd3aa643abb80fe1953668f67551.svg"/>

1324</div>

1325<p>

1326We also use your information to <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-ensure-working" data-name="ensure-working" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1327ensure our services are working as intended</a>

1328, such as tracking outages or troubleshooting issues that you report to us. And we use your information to <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-make-improvements" data-name="make-improvements" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1329make improvements</a>

1330 to our services — for example, understanding which search terms are most frequently misspelled helps us improve spell-check features used across our services.<h3>

1331Develop new services</h3>

1332<div class="pjyxF ">

1333<img class="zZLvvc" alt="" src="https://www.gstatic.com/policies/privacy/546f2b674b407304a2570e71a216e509.svg"/>

1334</div>

1335<p>

1336We use the information we collect in existing services to help us develop new ones. For example, understanding how people organized their photos in Picasa, Google’s first photos app, helped us design and launch Google Photos.</p>

1337<h3>

1338Provide personalized services, including content and ads</h3>

1339<div class="pjyxF ">

1340<img class="zZLvvc" alt="" src="https://www.gstatic.com/policies/privacy/51cd09d6239edc9652bc05ad1d149a5c.svg"/>

1341</div>

1342<p>

1343We use the information we collect to customize our services for you, including providing recommendations, personalized content, and <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-customized-search" data-name="customized-search" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1344customized search results</a>

1345. For example, <a href="https://myaccount.google.com/security-checkup?utm_source=pp" class="N6CPUe" target="_blank">

1346Security Checkup</a>

1347 provides security tips adapted to how you use Google products. And Google Play uses information like apps you’ve already installed and videos you’ve watched on YouTube to suggest new apps you might like.</p>

1348<p>

1349Depending on your settings, we may also show you <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-personalized-ads" data-name="personalized-ads" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1350personalized ads</a>

1351 based on your interests. For example, if you search for “mountain bikes,” you may see an ad for sports equipment when you’re browsing a site that shows ads served by Google. You can control what information we use to show you ads by visiting your ad settings.</p>

1352<ul>

1353<li>

1354We don’t show you personalized ads based on <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-sensitive-categories" data-name="sensitive-categories" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1355sensitive categories</a>

1356, such as race, religion, sexual orientation, or health.</li>

1357<li>

1358We don’t show you personalized ads based on your content from Drive, Gmail, or Photos.</li>

1359<li>

1360We don’t share information that personally identifies you with advertisers, such as your name or email, unless you ask us to. For example, if you see an ad for a nearby flower shop and select the “tap to call” button, we’ll connect your call and may share your phone number with the flower shop.</li>

1361</ul>

1362<div class="h0yEnd">

1363<div class="IN2z4b">

1364<img class="mZPFM " alt="" src="https://www.gstatic.com/policies/privacy/900a793eae04f4bddd675f8d95c4a794.svg"/>

1365</div>

1366<div class="gwGFXb">

1367<p class="n8ZyWe">

1368<a href="https://adssettings.google.com/?ref=privacy-policy" class="ky8S2">

1369Go to Ad Settings</a>

1370</p>

1371</div>

1372</div>

1373<h3>

1374Measure performance</h3>

1375<div class="pjyxF ">

1376<img class="zZLvvc" alt="" src="https://www.gstatic.com/policies/privacy/a8e78fa7fa279aa946fe1a9d6a0508f2.svg"/>

1377</div>

1378<p>

1379We use data for analytics and measurement to understand how our services are used. For example, we analyze data about your visits to our sites to do things like optimize product design. And we also use data about the ads you interact with to help advertisers understand the performance of their ad campaigns. We use a variety of tools to do this, including Google Analytics. When you visit sites that use Google Analytics, a Google Analytics customer may choose to enable Google to <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-link-info" data-name="link-info" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1380link information</a>

1381 about your activity from that site with activity from other sites that use our ad services.</p>

1382<h3>

1383Communicate with you</h3>

1384<div class="pjyxF ">

1385<img class="zZLvvc" alt="" src="https://www.gstatic.com/policies/privacy/acad335ad7ba163209d8c3e671b2c445.svg"/>

1386</div>

1387<p>

1388We use information we collect, like your email address, to interact with you directly. For example, we may send you a notification if we detect suspicious activity, like an attempt to sign in to your Google Account from an unusual location. Or we may let you know about upcoming changes or improvements to our services. And if you contact Google, we’ll keep a record of your request in order to help solve any issues you might be facing.</p>

1389<h3>

1390Protect Google, our users, and the public</h3>

1391<div class="pjyxF ">

1392<img class="zZLvvc" alt="" src="https://www.gstatic.com/policies/privacy/02f8664b95445de6f27ba682f3c5f9ab.svg"/>

1393</div>

1394<p>

1395We use information to help improve the <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-safety-reliability" data-name="safety-reliability" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1396safety and reliability</a>

1397 of our services. This includes detecting, preventing, and responding to fraud, abuse, security risks, and technical issues that could harm Google, our users, or the public.</p>

1398<hr/>

1399<p>

1400We use different technologies to process your information for these purposes. We use automated systems that analyze your content to provide you with things like customized search results, personalized ads, or other features tailored to how you use our services. And we analyze your content to help us <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-detect-abuse" data-name="detect-abuse" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1401detect abuse</a>

1402 such as spam, malware, and illegal content. We also use <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-algorithm" data-name="algorithm" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1403algorithms</a>

1404 to recognize patterns in data. For example, Google Translate helps people communicate across languages by detecting common language patterns in phrases you ask it to translate.</p>

1405<p>

1406We may <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-combine-info" data-name="combine-info" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1407combine the information we collect</a>

1408 among our services and across your devices for the purposes described above. For example, if you watch videos of guitar players on YouTube, you might see an ad for guitar lessons on a site that uses our ad products. Depending on your account settings, <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-other-sites" data-name="other-sites" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1409your activity on other sites and apps</a>

1410 may be associated with your personal information in order to improve Google’s services and the ads delivered by Google.</p>

1411<p>

1412If other users already have your email address or other information that identifies you, we may show them your publicly visible Google Account information, such as your name and photo. This helps people identify an email coming from you, for example.</p>

1413<p>

1414We’ll ask for your consent before using your information for a purpose that isn’t covered in this Privacy Policy.</p>

1604request to remove content</a>

1605 from specific Google services based on applicable law.</p>

1606<p>

1607To delete your information, you can:</p>

1608<ul>

1609<li>

1640 allows you to give someone else access to parts of your Google Account in case you’re unexpectedly unable to use your account.</p>

1647cookie</a>

1648 in your browser. You can also configure your browser to block all cookies from a specific domain or all domains. But remember that our services <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-rely-on-cookies" data-name="rely-on-cookies" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1649rely on cookies to function properly</a>

1650, for things like remembering your language preferences.</li>

1651<li>

1653modify location settings</a>

1654 on your Android device.</li>

1665<h1>

1666Sharing your information</h1>

1667<h2>

1668When you share your information</h2>

1669<p>

1670Many of our services let you share information with other people, and you have control over how you share. For example, you can share videos on YouTube publicly or you can decide to keep your videos private. Remember, when you share information publicly, your content may become accessible through search engines, including Google Search.</p>

1671<p>

1672When you’re signed in and interact with some Google services, like leaving comments on a YouTube video or reviewing an app in Play, your name and photo appear next to your activity. We may also display this information in <a href="https://support.google.com/accounts?p=privpol_endorse" class="N6CPUe" target="_blank">

1673ads depending on your Shared endorsements setting</a>

1674.</p>

1675<h2>

1676When Google shares your information</h2>

1677<p>

1678We do not share your personal information with companies, organizations, or individuals outside of Google except in the following cases:</p>

1679<h3>

1680With your consent</h3>

1681<p>

1682We’ll share personal information outside of Google when we have your consent. For example, if you <a href="https://support.google.com/googlehome?p=privpol_homedata" class="N6CPUe" target="_blank">

1683use Google Home to make a reservation</a>

1684 through a booking service, we’ll get your permission before sharing your name or phone number with the restaurant. We’ll ask for your explicit consent to share any <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-sensitive-info" data-name="sensitive-info" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1685sensitive personal information</a>

1686.</p>

1687<h3>

1688With domain administrators</h3>

1689<p>

1690If you’re a student or work for an organization that uses Google services, your <a href="https://support.google.com/a?p=privpol_admin" class="N6CPUe" target="_blank">

1691domain administrator</a>

1692 and resellers who manage your account will have access to your Google Account. They may be able to:</p>

1693<ul>

1694<li>

1695Access and retain information stored in your account, like your email</li>

1696<li>

1697View statistics regarding your account, like how many apps you install</li>

1698<li>

1699Change your account password</li>

1700<li>

1701Suspend or terminate your account access</li>

1702<li>

1703Receive your account information in order to satisfy applicable law, regulation, legal process, or enforceable governmental request</li>

1704<li>

1705Restrict your ability to delete or edit your information or your privacy settings</li>

1706</ul>

1707<h3>

1708For external processing</h3>

1709<p>

1710We provide personal information to our <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-affiliates" data-name="affiliates" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1711affiliates</a>

1712 and other trusted businesses or persons to process it for us, based on our instructions and in compliance with our Privacy Policy and any other appropriate confidentiality and security measures. For example, we use service providers to help us with customer support.</p>

1713<h3>

1714For legal reasons</h3>

1715<p>

1716We will share personal information outside of Google if we have a good-faith belief that access, use, preservation, or disclosure of the information is reasonably necessary to:</p>

1717<ul>

1718<li>

1719Meet any applicable law, regulation, <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-legal" data-name="legal" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1720legal process, or enforceable governmental request</a>

1721. We share information about the number and type of requests we receive from governments in our <a href="https://transparencyreport.google.com/user-data/overview" class="N6CPUe" target="_blank">

1722Transparency Report</a>

1723.</li>

1724<li>

1725Enforce applicable Terms of Service, including investigation of potential violations.</li>

1726<li>

1727Detect, prevent, or otherwise address fraud, security, or technical issues.</li>

1728<li>

1729Protect against harm to the rights, property or safety of Google, our users, or the public as required or permitted by law.</li>

1730</ul>

1731<p>

1732We may share <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-info" data-name="info" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1733non-personally identifiable information</a>

1734 publicly and with our partners — like publishers, advertisers, developers, or rights holders. For example, we share information publicly to <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-trends" data-name="trends" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1735show trends</a>

1736 about the general use of our services. We also allow <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-specific-partners" data-name="specific-partners" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1737specific partners</a>

1738 to collect information from your browser or device for advertising and measurement purposes using their own cookies or similar technologies.</p>

1739<p>

1740If Google is involved in a merger, acquisition, or sale of assets, we’ll continue to ensure the confidentiality of your personal information and give affected users notice before personal information is transferred or becomes subject to a different privacy policy.</p>

1750<h1>

1752<p class="vxK8q">

1753We build security into our services to protect your information</p>

1754<p>

1755All Google products are built with strong security features that continuously protect your information. The insights we gain from maintaining our services help us detect and automatically block security threats from ever reaching you. And if we do detect something risky that we think you should know about, we’ll notify you and help guide you through steps to stay better protected.</p>

1756<p>

1757We work hard to protect you and Google from unauthorized access, alteration, disclosure, or destruction of information we hold, including:</p>

1758<ul>

1759<li>

1760We use encryption to keep your data private while in transit</li>

1761<li>

1762We offer a range of security features, like <a href="https://safebrowsing.google.com/?utm_source=pp" class="N6CPUe" target="_blank">

1763Safe Browsing</a>

1764, Security Checkup, and <a href="https://www.google.com/landing/2step/?utm_source=pp" class="N6CPUe" target="_blank">

17652 Step Verification</a>

1766 to help you protect your account</li>

1767<li>

1768We review our information collection, storage, and processing practices, including physical security measures, to prevent unauthorized access to our systems</li>

1769<li>

1770We restrict access to personal information to Google employees, contractors, and agents who need that information in order to process it. Anyone with this access is subject to strict contractual confidentiality obligations and may be disciplined or terminated if they fail to meet these obligations.</li>

1771</ul>

1835<h1>

1836Retaining your information</h1>

1837<p>

1838We retain the data we collect for different periods of time depending on what it is, how we use it, and how you configure your settings:</p>

1839<ul>

1840<li>

1841Some data you can delete whenever you like, such as the content you create or upload. You can also delete <a href="https://myactivity.google.com/myactivity" class="N6CPUe" target="_blank">

1842activity information</a>

1843 saved in your account, or <a href="https://support.google.com/accounts/answer/465?authuser=0#auto-delete" class="N6CPUe" target="_blank">

1844choose to have it deleted automatically</a>

1845 after a set period of time.</li>

1846<li>

1847Other data is deleted or anonymized automatically after a set period of time, such as <a href="technologies/ads">

1848advertising data</a>

1849 in server logs.</li>

1850<li>

1851We keep some data until you delete your Google Account, such as information about how often you use our services.</li>

1852<li>

1853And some data we retain for longer periods of time when necessary for legitimate business or legal purposes, such as security, fraud and abuse prevention, or financial record-keeping.</li>

1854</ul>

1855<p>

1856When you delete data, we follow a deletion process to make sure that your data is safely and completely removed from our servers or retained only in anonymized form. We try to ensure that our services protect information from accidental or malicious deletion. Because of this, there may be delays between when you delete something and when copies are deleted from our active and backup systems.</p>

1857<p>

1858You can read more about Google’s <a href="technologies/retention">

1859data retention periods</a>

1860, including how long it takes us to delete your information.</p>

1874<h2>

1875Data transfers</h2>

1876<p>

1877We maintain <a class="g1mG8c" href="privacy#footnote-servers" data-name="servers" jsaction="click:IPbaae(preventDefault=true)">

1878servers around the world</a>

1879 and your information may be processed on servers located outside of the country where you live. Data protection laws vary among countries, with some providing more protection than others. Regardless of where your information is processed, we apply the same protections described in this policy. We also comply with certain <a href="privacy/frameworks">

1880legal frameworks</a>

1881 relating to the transfer of data.</p>

1882<p>

1883When we receive formal written complaints, we respond by contacting the person who made the complaint. We work with the appropriate regulatory authorities, including local data protection authorities, to resolve any complaints regarding the transfer of your data that we cannot resolve with you directly.</p>

2018<h2>

2019Key terms</h2>

2020<h3 id="footnote-affiliates">

2021Affiliates</h3>

2022<p>

2023An affiliate is an entity that belongs to the Google group of companies, including the following companies that provide consumer services in the EU: Google Ireland Limited, Google Commerce Ltd, Google Payment Corp, and Google Dialer Inc. Learn more about the <a href="https://privacy.google.com/businesses/affiliates">

2024companies providing business services in the EU</a>

2025.</p>

2026<h3 id="footnote-algorithm">

2027Algorithm</h3>

2028<p>

2029A process or set of rules followed by a computer in performing problem-solving operations.</p>

2030<h3 id="footnote-application-data-cache">

2031Application data cache</h3>

2032<p>

2033An application data cache is a data repository on a device. It can, for example, enable a web application to run without an internet connection and improve the performance of the application by enabling faster loading of content.</p>

2034<h3 id="footnote-browser-storage">

2035Browser web storage</h3>

2036<p>

2037Browser web storage enables websites to store data in a browser on a device. When used in "local storage" mode, it enables data to be stored across sessions. This makes data retrievable even after a browser has been closed and reopened. One technology that facilitates web storage is HTML 5.</p>

2038<h3 id="footnote-cookies">

2039Cookies</h3>

2040<p>

2041A cookie is a small file containing a string of characters that is sent to your computer when you visit a website. When you visit the site again, the cookie allows that site to recognize your browser. Cookies may store user preferences and other information. You can configure your browser to refuse all cookies or to indicate when a cookie is being sent. However, some website features or services may not function properly without cookies. Learn more about <a href="technologies/cookies">

2042how Google uses cookies</a>

2043 and how Google uses data, including cookies, <a href="technologies/partner-sites">

2044when you use our partners' sites or apps</a>

2045.</p>

2046<h3 id="footnote-device">

2047Device</h3>

2048<p>

2049A device is a computer that can be used to access Google services. For example, desktop computers, tablets, smart speakers, and smartphones are all considered devices.</p>

2050<h3 id="footnote-account">

2051Google Account</h3>

2052<p>

2053You may access some of our services by signing up for a <a href="https://myaccount.google.com/">

2054Google Account</a>

2055 and providing us with some personal information (typically your name, email address, and a password). This account information is used to authenticate you when you access Google services and protect your account from unauthorized access by others. You can edit or delete your account at any time through your Google Account settings.</p>

2056<h3 id="footnote-ip">

2057IP address</h3>

2058<p>

2059Every device connected to the Internet is assigned a number known as an Internet protocol (IP) address. These numbers are usually assigned in geographic blocks. An IP address can often be used to identify the location from which a device is connecting to the Internet.</p>

2060<h3 id="footnote-info">

2061Non-personally identifiable information</h3>

2062<p>

2063This is information that is recorded about users so that it no longer reflects or references an individually-identifiable user.</p>

2064<h3 id="footnote-personal-info">

2065Personal information</h3>

2066<p>

2067This is information that you provide to us which personally identifies you, such as your name, email address, or billing information, or other data that can be reasonably linked to such information by Google, such as information we associate with your Google Account.</p>

2068<h3 id="footnote-pixel">

2069Pixel tag</h3>

2070<p>

2071A pixel tag is a type of technology placed on a website or within the body of an email for the purpose of tracking certain activity, such as views of a website or when an email is opened. Pixel tags are often used in combination with cookies.</p>

2072<h3 id="footnote-referrer-url">

2073Referrer URL</h3>

2074<p>

2075A Referrer URL (Uniform Resource Locator) is information transmitted to a destination webpage by a web browser, typically when you click a link to that page. The Referrer URL contains the URL of the last webpage the browser visited.</p>

2076<h3 id="footnote-sensitive-info">

2077Sensitive personal information</h3>

2078<p>

2079This is a particular category of personal information relating to topics such as confidential medical facts, racial or ethnic origins, political or religious beliefs, or sexuality.</p>

2080<h3 id="footnote-server-logs">

2081Server logs</h3>

2082<p>

2083Like most websites, our servers automatically record the page requests made when you visit our sites. These “server logs” typically include your web request, Internet Protocol address, browser type, browser language, the date and time of your request, and one or more cookies that may uniquely identify your browser.</p>

2084<p>

2085A typical log entry for a search for “cars” looks like this:</p>

2086<pre>

2087123.45.67.89 - 25/Mar/2003 10:15:32 -<br>

2088http&#58;//www.google.com/search?q=cars -<br>

2089Firefox 1.0.7; Windows NT 5.1 -<br>

2090740674ce2123e969</pre>

2091<ul>

2092<li>

2093<code>

2094123.45.67.89</code>

2095 is the Internet Protocol address assigned to the user by the user’s ISP. Depending on the user’s service, a different address may be assigned to the user by their service provider each time they connect to the Internet.</li>

2096<li>

2097<code>

209825/Mar/2003 10:15:32</code>

2099 is the date and time of the query.</li>

2100<li>

2101<code>

2102http&#58;//www.google.com/search?q=cars</code>

2103 is the requested URL, including the search query.</li>

2104<li>

2105<code>

2106Firefox 1.0.7; Windows NT 5.1</code>

2107 is the browser and operating system being used.</li>

2108<li>

2109<code>

2110740674ce2123a969</code>

2111 is the unique cookie ID assigned to this particular computer the first time it visited Google. (Cookies can be deleted by users. If the user has deleted the cookie from the computer since the last time they’ve visited Google, then it will be the unique cookie ID assigned to their device the next time they visit Google from that particular device).</li>

2112</ul>

2113<h3 id="footnote-unique-id">

2114Unique identifiers</h3>

2115<p>

2116A unique identifier is a string of characters that can be used to uniquely identify a browser, app, or device. Different identifiers vary in how permanent they are, whether they can be reset by users, and how they can be accessed.</p>

2117<p>

2118Unique identifiers can be used for various purposes, including security and fraud detection, syncing services such as your email inbox, remembering your preferences, and providing personalized advertising. For example, unique identifiers stored in cookies help sites display content in your browser in your preferred language. You can configure your browser to refuse all cookies or to indicate when a cookie is being sent. Learn more about <a href="technologies/cookies">

2119how Google uses cookies</a>

2120.</p>

2121<p>

2122On other platforms besides browsers, unique identifiers are used to recognize a specific device or app on that device. For example, a unique identifier such as the Advertising ID is used to provide relevant advertising on Android devices, and can be <a href="technologies/ads">

2123managed</a>

2124 in your device’s settings. Unique identifiers may also be incorporated into a device by its manufacturer (sometimes called a universally unique ID or UUID), such as the IMEI-number of a mobile phone. For example, a device’s unique identifier can be used to customize our service to your device or analyze device issues related to our services.</p>

2125<h2>

2126Additional Context</h2>

2127<h3 id="footnote-useful-ads">

2128ads you’ll find most useful</h3>

2129<p>

2130For example, if you watch videos about baking on YouTube, you may see more ads that relate to baking as you browse the web. We also may use your IP address to determine your approximate location, so that we can serve you ads for a nearby pizza delivery service if you search for “pizza.” Learn more <a href="https://support.google.com/accounts?p=privpol_whyad">

2131about Google ads</a>

2132 and <a href="https://support.google.com/accounts?p=privpol_whyad">

2133why you may see particular ads</a>

2134.</p>

2135<h3 id="footnote-ad-services">

2136advertising and research services on their behalf</h3>

2137<p>

2138For example, advertisers may upload data from their loyalty-card programs so that they can better understand the performance of their ad campaigns. We only provide aggregated reports to advertisers that don’t reveal information about individual people.</p>

2139<h3 id="footnote-android-device">

2140Android device with Google apps</h3>

2141<p>

2142Android devices with Google apps include devices sold by Google or one of our partners and include phones, cameras, vehicles, wearables, and televisions. These devices use Google Play Services and other pre-installed apps that include services like Gmail, Maps, your phone’s camera and phone dialer, text-to-speech conversion, keyboard input, and security features.</p>

2143<h3 id="footnote-combine-info">

2144combine the information we collect</h3>

2145<p>

2146Some examples of how we combine the information we collect include:</p>

2147<ul>

2148<li>

2149When you’re signed in to your Google Account and search on Google, you can see search results from the public web, along with relevant information from the content you have in other Google products, like Gmail or Google Calendar. This can include things like the status of your upcoming flights, restaurant, and hotel reservations, or your photos. <a href="https://support.google.com/websearch?p=privpol_privresults&amp;hl=en" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">

2150Learn more</a>

2151</li>

2152<li>

2153If you have communicated with someone via Gmail and want to add them to a Google Doc or an event in Google Calendar, Google makes it easy to do so by autocompleting their email address when you start to type in their name. This feature makes it easier to share things with people you know. <a href="https://support.google.com/accounts?p=autocontacts&amp;hl=en" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">

2154Learn more</a>

2155</li>

2156<li>

2157The Google app can use data that you have stored in other Google products to show you personalized content, depending on your settings. For example, if you have searches stored in your Web & App Activity, the Google app can show you news articles and other information about your interests, like sports scores, based your activity. <a href="https://support.google.com/websearch?p=privpol_feed&amp;hl=en" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">

2158Learn more</a>

2159</li>

2160<li>

2161If you link your Google Account to your Google Home, you can manage your information and get things done through the Google Assistant. For example, you can add events to your Google Calendar or get your schedule for the day, ask for status updates on your upcoming flight, or send information like driving directions to your phone. <a href="https://support.google.com/googlehome?p=privpol_actions&amp;hl=en" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">

2162Learn more</a>

2163</li>

2164</ul>

2165<h3 id="footnote-customized-search">

2166customized search results</h3>

2167<p>

2168For example, when you’re signed in to your Google Account and have the Web & App Activity control enabled, you can get more relevant search results that are based on your previous searches and activity from other Google services. You can <a href="https://support.google.com/websearch?p=privpol_searchactivity">

2169learn more here</a>

2170. You may also get customized search results even when you’re signed out. If you don’t want this level of search customization, you can <a href="https://support.google.com/websearch?p=privpol_incognito">

2171search and browse privately</a>

2172 or turn off <a href="https://www.google.com/history/optout?utm_source=pp">

2173signed-out search personalization</a>

2174.</p>

2175<h3 id="footnote-deliver-services">

2176deliver our services</h3>

2177<p>

2178Examples of how we use your information to deliver our services include:</p>

2179<ul>

2180<li>

2181We use the IP address assigned to your device to send you the data you requested, such as loading a YouTube video</li>

2182<li>

2183We use unique identifiers stored in cookies on your device to help us authenticate you as the person who should have access to your Google Account</li>

2184<li>

2185Photos and videos you upload to Google Photos are used to help you create albums, animations, and other creations that you can share. <a href="https://support.google.com/photos?p=privpol_manage">

2186Learn more</a>

2187</li>

2188<li>

2189A flight confirmation email you receive may be used to create a “check-in” button that appears in your Gmail</li>

2190<li>

2191When you purchase services or physical goods from us, you may provide us information like your shipping address or delivery instructions. We use this information for things like processing, fulfilling, and delivering your order, and to provide support in connection with the product or service you purchase.</li>

2192</ul>

2193<h3 id="footnote-detect-abuse">

2194detect abuse</h3>

2195<p>

2196When we detect spam, malware, illegal content, and other forms of abuse on our systems in violation of our policies, we may disable your account or take other appropriate action. In certain circumstances, we may also report the violation to appropriate authorities.</p>

2197<h3 id="footnote-devices">

2198devices</h3>

2199<p>

2200For example, we can use information from your devices to help you decide which device you’d like to use to install an app or view a movie you buy from Google Play. We also use this information to help protect your account.</p>

2201<h3 id="footnote-improve">

2202ensure and improve</h3>

2203<p>

2204For example, we analyze how people interact with advertising to improve the performance of our ads.</p>

2205<h3 id="footnote-ensure-working">

2206ensure our services are working as intended</h3>

2207<p>

2208For example, we continuously monitor our systems to look for problems. And if we find something wrong with a specific feature, reviewing activity information collected before the problem started allows us to fix things more quickly.</p>

2209<h3 id="footnote-near-device">

2210Information about things near your device</h3>

2211<p>

2212If you use Google’s Location services on Android, we can improve the performance of apps that rely on your location, like Google Maps. If you use Google’s Location services, your device sends information to Google about its location, sensors (like accelerometer), and nearby cell towers and Wi-Fi access points (like MAC address and signal strength). All these things help to determine your location. You can use your device settings to enable Google Location services. <a href="https://support.google.com/accounts?p=privpol_androidloc&amp;hl=en" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">

2213Learn more</a>

2214</p>

2215<h3 id="footnote-legal">

2216legal process, or enforceable governmental request</h3>

2217<p>

2218Like other technology and communications companies, Google regularly receives requests from governments and courts around the world to disclose user data. Respect for the privacy and security of data you store with Google underpins our approach to complying with these legal requests. Our legal team reviews each and every request, regardless of type, and we frequently push back when a request appears to be overly broad or doesn’t follow the correct process. Learn more in our <a href="https://transparencyreport.google.com/user-data/overview">

2219Transparency Report</a>

2220.</p>

2221<h3 id="footnote-make-improvements">

2222make improvements</h3>

2223<p>

2224For example, we use cookies to analyze how people interact with our services. And that analysis can help us build better products. For example, it may help us discover that it’s taking people too long to complete a certain task or that they have trouble finishing steps at all. We can then redesign that feature and improve the product for everyone.</p>

2225<h3 id="footnote-link-info">

2226may link information</h3>

2227<p>

2228Google Analytics relies on first-party cookies, which means the cookies are set by the Google Analytics customer. Using our systems, data generated through Google Analytics can be linked by the Google Analytics customer and by Google to third-party cookies that are related to visits to other websites. For example, an advertiser may want to use its Google Analytics data to create more relevant ads, or to further analyze its traffic. <a href="https://support.google.com/analytics?p=privpol_data&amp;hl=en" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">

2229Learn more</a>

2230</p>

2231<h3 id="footnote-partner">

2232partner with Google</h3>

2233<p>

2234There are over 2 million non-Google websites and apps that partner with Google to show ads. <a href="https://support.google.com/accounts?p=privpol_controlads&amp;hl=en" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">

2235Learn more</a>

2236</p>

2237<h3 id="footnote-payment-info">

2238payment information</h3>

2239<p>

2240For example, if you add a credit card or other payment method to your Google Account, you can use it to buy things across our services, like apps in the Play Store. We may also ask for other information, like a business tax ID, to help process your payment. In some cases, we may also need to verify your identity and may ask you for information to do this.</p>

2241<p>

2242We may also use payment information to verify that you meet age requirements, if, for example, you enter an incorrect birthday indicating you’re not old enough to have a Google Account. <a href="https://support.google.com/accounts?p=privpol_agereq&amp;hl=en" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">

2243Learn more</a>

2244</p>

2245<h3 id="footnote-personalized-ads">

2246personalized ads</h3>

2247<p>

2248You may also see personalized ads based on information from the advertiser. If you shopped on an advertiser's website, for example, they can use that visit information to show you ads. <a href="https://support.google.com/accounts?p=privpol_whyad&amp;hl=en" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">

2249Learn more</a>

2250</p>

2251<h3 id="footnote-phone-number">

2252phone number</h3>

2253<p>

2254If you add your phone number to your account, it can be used for different purposes across Google services, depending on your settings. For example, your phone number can be used to help you access your account if you forget your password, help people find and connect with you, and make the ads you see more relevant to you. <a href="https://support.google.com/accounts?p=privpol_phone&amp;hl=en" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">

2255Learn more</a>

2256</p>

2257<h3 id="footnote-against-abuse">

2258protect against abuse</h3>

2259<p>

2260For example, information about security threats can help us notify you if we think your account has been compromised (at which point we can help you take steps to protect your account).</p>

2261<h3 id="footnote-sources">

2262publicly accessible sources</h3>

2263<p>

2264For example, we may collect information that’s publicly available online or from other public sources to help train Google’s language models and build features like Google Translate. Or, if your business’s information appears on a website, we may index and display it on Google services.</p>

2265<h3 id="footnote-rely-on-cookies">

2266rely on cookies to function properly</h3>

2267<p>

2268For example, we use a cookie called ‘lbcs’ that makes it possible for you to open many Google Docs in one browser. Blocking this cookie would prevent Google Docs from working as expected. <a href="technologies/cookies#types-of-cookies">

2269Learn more</a>

2270</p>

2271<h3 id="footnote-safety-reliability">

2272safety and reliability</h3>

2273<p>

2274Some examples of how we use your information to help keep our services safe and reliable include:</p>

2275<ul>

2276<li>

2277Collecting and analyzing IP addresses and cookie data to protect against automated abuse. This abuse takes many forms, such as sending spam to Gmail users, stealing money from advertisers by fraudulently clicking on ads, or censoring content by launching a Distributed Denial of Service (DDoS) attack.</li>

2278<li>

2279The “last account activity” feature in Gmail can help you find out if and when someone accessed your email without your knowledge. This feature shows you information about recent activity in Gmail, such as the IP addresses that accessed your mail, the associated location, and the date and time of access. <a href="https://support.google.com/mail?p=privpol_signinactivity&amp;hl=en" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">

2280Learn more</a>

2281</li>

2282</ul>

2283<h3 id="footnote-sensitive-categories">

2284sensitive categories</h3>

2285<p>

2286When showing you personalized ads, we use topics that we think might be of interest to you based on your activity. For example, you may see ads for things like "Cooking and Recipes" or "Air Travel.” We don’t use topics or show personalized ads based on sensitive categories like race, religion, sexual orientation, or health. And we <a href="https://support.google.com/adwordspolicy?p=privpol_p13nad">

2287require the same from advertisers</a>

2288 that use our services.</p>

2289<h3 id="footnote-sensor-data">

2290Sensor data from your device</h3>

2291<p>

2292Your device may have sensors that can be used to better understand your location and movement. For example, an accelerometer can be used to determine your speed and a gyroscope to figure out your direction of travel.</p>

2293<h3 id="footnote-servers">

2294servers around the world</h3>

2295<p>

2296For example, we operate data centers located <a href="https://www.google.com/about/datacenters/inside/locations">

2297around the world</a>

2298 to help keep our products continuously available for users.</p>

2299<h3 id="footnote-calls-messages">

2300services to make and receive calls or send and receive messages</h3>

2301<p>

2302Examples of these services include:</p>

2303<ul>

2304<li>

2305Google Voice, for making and receiving calls, sending text messages, and managing voicemail</li>

2306<li>

2307Google Meet, for making and receiving video calls</li>

2308<li>

2309Gmail, for sending and receiving emails</li>

2310<li>

2311Google Chat, for sending and receiving messages</li>

2312<li>

2313Google Duo, for making and receiving video calls and sending and receiving messages</li>

2314<li>

2315Google Fi, for a phone plan</li>

2316</ul>

2317<h3 id="footnote-trends">

2318show trends</h3>

2319<p>

2320When lots of people start searching for something, it can provide useful information about particular trends at that time. Google Trends samples Google web searches to estimate the popularity of searches over a certain period of time and shares those results publicly in aggregated terms. <a href="https://support.google.com/trends?p=privpol_about">

2321Learn more</a>

2322</p>

2323<h3 id="footnote-delete-specific">

2324specific Google services</h3>

2325<p>

2326For example, you can delete <a href="https://support.google.com/blogger?p=privpol_blog">

2327your blog</a>

2328 from Blogger or <a href="https://support.google.com/sites?p=privpol_delete">

2329a Google Site you own</a>

2330 from Google Sites. You can also delete <a href="https://support.google.com/googleplay?p=privpol_review">

2331reviews</a>

2332 you’ve left on apps, games, and other content in the Play Store.</p>

2333<h3 id="footnote-specific-partners">

2334specific partners</h3>

2335<p>

2336For example, we allow YouTube creators and advertisers to work with measurement companies to learn about the audience of their YouTube videos or ads, using cookies or similar technologies. Another example is merchants on our shopping pages, who use cookies to understand how many different people see their product listings. <a href="privacy/google-partners">

2337Learn more</a>

2338 about these partners and how they use your information.</p>

2339<h3 id="footnote-chrome-sync">

2340synced with your Google Account</h3>

2341<p>

2342Your Chrome browsing history is only saved to your account if you’ve enabled Chrome synchronization with your Google Account. <a href="https://support.google.com/chrome?p=privpol_chrsync">

2343Learn more</a>

2344</p>

2345<h3 id="footnote-people-online">

2346the people who matter most to you online</h3>

2347<p>

2348For example, when you type an address in the To, Cc, or Bcc field of an email you're composing, Gmail will suggest addresses based on the people you <a href="https://contacts.google.com">

2349contact most frequently</a>

2350.</p>

2351<h3 id="footnote-third-parties">

2352third parties</h3>

2353<p>

2354For example, we process your information to report use statistics to rights holders about how their content was used in our services. We may also process your information if people search for your name and we display search results for sites containing publicly available information about you.</p>

2355<h3 id="footnote-content-views">

2356Views and interactions with content and ads</h3>

2357<p>

2358For example, we collect information about views and interactions with ads so we can provide aggregated reports to advertisers, like telling them whether we served their ad on a page and whether the ad was likely seen by a viewer. We may also measure other interactions, such as how you move your mouse over an ad or if you interact with the page on which the ad appears.</p>

2359<h3 id="footnote-other-sites">

2360your activity on other sites and apps</h3>

2361<p>

2362This activity might come from your use of Google services, like from syncing your account with Chrome or your visits to sites and apps that partner with Google. Many websites and apps partner with Google to improve their content and services. For example, a website might use our advertising services (like AdSense) or analytics tools (like Google Analytics), or it might embed other content (such as videos from YouTube). These services may share information about your activity with Google and, depending on your <a href="https://myaccount.google.com/">

2363account settings</a>

2364 and the products in use (for instance, when a partner uses Google Analytics in conjunction with our advertising services), this data may be associated with your personal information.</p>

2365<p>

2366<a href="technologies/partner-sites">

2367Learn more</a>

2368 about how Google uses data when you use our partners' sites or apps.</p>
